with the exception of a few vehicle-specific payloads that are delivered on the European <a href="/wiki/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle" title="Automated Transfer Vehicle">ATV</a> and the Japanese <a href="/wiki/H-II_Transfer_Vehicle" title="H-II Transfer Vehicle">HTV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup></p>\n<h5><span id="Commercial_Crew_Program_(2010\xe2\x80\x93present)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_Crew_Program_.282010.E2.80.93present.29">Commercial Crew Program (2010\xe2\x80\x93present)</span></h5>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development" title="Commercial Crew Development">Commercial Crew Development</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development" title="Commercial Crew Development">Commercial Crew Development</a> (CCDev) program was initiated in 2010 with the purpose of creating American commercially operated crewed spacecraft capable of delivering at least four crew members to the ISS, staying docked for 180 days and then returning them back to Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Berger_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Berger-99">[98]</a></sup> It is hoped that these vehicles could also transport non-NASA customers to private space stations such those planned by <a href="/wiki/Bigelow_Aerospace" title="Bigelow Aerospace">Bigelow Aerospace</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> Like COTS, CCDev is also a fixed price milestone-based developmental program that requires some private investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasaRendezvous2010-2_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-nasaRendezvous2010-2-92">[91]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2010, NASA announced the winners of the first phase of the program, a total of $50\xc2\xa0million was divided among five American companies to foster research and development into human spaceflight concepts and technologies in the private sector. In 2011, the winners of the second phase of the program were announced, $270\xc2\xa0million was divided among four companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ft20110418_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-ft20110418-101">[100]</a></sup> In 2012, the winners of the third phase of the program were announced, NASA provided $1.1 billion divided among three companies to further develop their crew transportation systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-August2012_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-August2012-102">[101]</a></sup> In 2014, the winners of the final round were announced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CCtCapBlogAnnounce_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-CCtCapBlogAnnounce-103">[102]</a></sup> SpaceX\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dragon_V2" title="Dragon V2">Dragon V2</a> (planned to be launched on a <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9_v1.1" title="Falcon 9 v1.1">Falcon 9 v1.1</a>) received a contract valued up to $2.6 billion and Boeing\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CST-100" title="CST-100">CST-100</a> (to be launched on an <a href="/wiki/Atlas_V" title="Atlas V">Atlas V</a>) received a contract valued up to $4.2 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20140921_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-sn20140921-104">[103]</a></sup> NASA expects these vehicles to begin transporting humans to the ISS in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20140921_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-sn20140921-104">[103]</a></sup></p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px">\n<div style="width: 182px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;">\n<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_(16661791299).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg/270px-SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg/405px-SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg/540px-SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div>\n</div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Dragon V2</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">\n<div style="width: 162px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">\n<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CST-100.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2250" data-file-width="3000" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/CST-100.jpg/240px-CST-100.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/CST-100.jpg/360px-CST-100.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/CST-100.jpg/480px-CST-100.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a></div>\n</div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Computer rendering of CST-100 in orbit</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<h4><span id="Beyond_Low_Earth_Orbit_program_(2010\xe2\x80\x93present)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Beyond_Low_Earth_Orbit_program_.282010.E2.80.93present.29">Beyond Low Earth Orbit program (2010\xe2\x80\x93present)</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="2880" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg/170px-Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg/255px-Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg/340px-Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Art_of_SLS_launch.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nArtist\'s rendering of the 70 mt variant of SLS launching Orion</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>For missions beyond <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">low Earth orbit</a> (BLEO), NASA has been directed to develop the <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">Space Launch System</a> (SLS), a Saturn-V class rocket, and the two to six person, beyond low Earth orbit spacecraft, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_spacecraft" title="Orion spacecraft">Orion</a>. In February 2010, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>\'s administration proposed eliminating public funds for the <a href="/wiki/Constellation_program" title="Constellation program">Constellation program</a> and shifting greater responsibility of servicing the ISS to private companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Achenbach_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Achenbach-105">[104]</a></sup> During a speech at the Kennedy Space Center on April 15, 2010, Obama proposed a new heavy-lift vehicle (HLV) to replace the formerly planned <a href="/wiki/Ares_V" title="Ares V">Ares V</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-speech_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-speech-106">[105]</a></sup> In his speech, Obama called for a manned mission to an asteroid as soon as 2025, and a manned mission to Mars orbit by the mid-2030s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-speech_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-speech-106">[105]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/NASA_Authorization_Act_of_2010" title="NASA Authorization Act of 2010">NASA Authorization Act of 2010</a> was passed by Congress and signed into law on October 11, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa2010_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa2010-107">[106]</a></sup> The act officially canceled the Constellation program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa2010_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-nasa2010-107">[106]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Authorization Act required a newly designed HLV be chosen within 90 days of its passing; the launch vehicle was given the name "Space Launch System". The new law also required the construction of a beyond low earth orbit spacecraft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_spacecraft" title="Orion spacecraft">Orion spacecraft</a>, which was being developed as part of the Constellation program, was chosen to fulfill this role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-authorizationact_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-authorizationact-109">[108]</a></sup> The Space Launch System is planned to launch both Orion and other necessary hardware for missions beyond low Earth orbit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> The SLS is to be upgraded over time with more powerful versions. The initial capability of SLS is required to be able to lift 70 mt into <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">LEO</a>. It is then planned to be upgraded to 105 mt and then eventually to 130 mt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-authorizationact_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-authorizationact-109">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schedule_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-111">[110]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Exploration_Flight_Test_1" title="Exploration Flight Test 1">Exploration Flight Test 1</a> (EFT-1), an unmanned test flight of Orion\'s crew module, was launched on December 5, 2014, atop a <a href="/wiki/Delta_IV_Heavy" title="Delta IV Heavy">Delta IV Heavy</a> rocket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schedule_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-111">[110]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Exploration_Mission_1" title="Exploration Mission 1">Exploration Mission-1</a> (EM-1) is the unmanned initial launch of SLS that would also send Orion on a <a href="/wiki/Circumlunar_trajectory" title="Circumlunar trajectory">circumlunar trajectory</a>, which is planned for 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schedule_111-2"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-111">[110]</a></sup> The first manned flight of Orion and SLS, Exploration Mission 2 (EM-2) is to launch in 2022; it is a 10- to 14-day mission planned to place a crew of four into <a href="/wiki/Lunar_orbit" title="Lunar orbit">Lunar orbit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schedule_111-3"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-111">[110]</a></sup> EM-3 is planned to deliver a crew of 4 to <a href="/wiki/Lunar_orbit" title="Lunar orbit">Lunar orbit</a> along with the first module of <a href="/wiki/Deep_Space_Gateway" title="Deep Space Gateway">Deep Space Gateway</a>.</p>\n<p>On June 5, 2016, NASA and DARPA announced plans to build a series of new X-planes over the next 10 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Building_X_Planes_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Building_X_Planes-112">[111]</a></sup> One of the planes will reportedly be a supersonic vehicle that burns low-carbon <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biofuels" title="Biofuels">biofuels</a> and generates quiet sonic booms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Building_X_Planes_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-Building_X_Planes-112">[111]</a></sup></p>\n<p>NASA plans to build full scale deep space habitats such at the <a href="/wiki/Nautilus-X" title="Nautilus-X">Nautilus-X</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deep_Space_Gateway" title="Deep Space Gateway">Deep Space Gateway</a> as part of its <a href="/wiki/Next_Space_Technologies_for_Exploration_Partnerships" title="Next Space Technologies for Exploration Partnerships">Next Space Technologies for Exploration Partnerships</a> (NextSTEP) program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unmanned_programs">Unmanned programs</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pioneer-3-4.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="300" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pioneer-3-4.gif/170px-Pioneer-3-4.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pioneer-3-4.gif/255px-Pioneer-3-4.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0e/Pioneer-3-4.gif 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pioneer-3-4.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<i><a href="/wiki/Pioneer_3" title="Pioneer 3">Pioneer 3</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_4" title="Pioneer 4"><i>4</i></a> launched in 1958 and 1959, respectively</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1560" data-file-width="1041" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg/220px-JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg/330px-JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg/440px-JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JWST_Full_Mirror.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nJWST main mirror assembled, November 2016</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_NASA_missions" title="Unmanned NASA missions">Unmanned NASA missions</a></div>\n<p>More than 1,000 unmanned missions have been designed to explore the Earth and the solar system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAHisStat_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAHisStat-114">[113]</a></sup> Besides exploration, communication satellites have also been launched by NASA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAHis6_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAHis6-115">[114]</a></sup> The missions have been launched directly from Earth or from orbiting space shuttles, which could either deploy the satellite itself, or with a rocket stage to take it farther.</p>\n<p>The first US unmanned satellite was <a href="/wiki/Explorer_1" title="Explorer 1">Explorer 1</a>, which started as an ABMA/JPL project during the early part of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a>. It was launched in January 1958, two months after Sputnik. At the creation of NASA the Explorer project was transferred to this agency and still continues to this day. Its missions have been focusing on the Earth and the Sun, measuring magnetic fields and the <a href="/wiki/Solar_wind" title="Solar wind">solar wind</a>, among other aspects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAExp_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAExp-116">[115]</a></sup> A more recent Earth mission, not related to the Explorer program, was the <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a>, which as mentioned above was brought into orbit in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inner_Solar_System" title="Inner Solar System">inner Solar System</a> has been made the goal of at least four unmanned programs. The first was <a href="/wiki/Mariner_program" title="Mariner program">Mariner</a> in the 1960s and \'70s, which made multiple visits to <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> and one to <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a>. Probes launched under the Mariner program were also the first to make a planetary flyby (<a href="/wiki/Mariner_2" title="Mariner 2">Mariner 2</a>), to take the first pictures from another planet (<a href="/wiki/Mariner_4" title="Mariner 4">Mariner 4</a>), the first planetary orbiter (<a href="/wiki/Mariner_9" title="Mariner 9">Mariner 9</a>), and the first to make a <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">gravity assist</a> maneuver (<a href="/wiki/Mariner_10" title="Mariner 10">Mariner 10</a>). This is a technique where the satellite takes advantage of the gravity and velocity of planets to reach its destination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JPL_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-JPL-118">[117]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The first successful landing on Mars was made by <i><a href="/wiki/Viking_1" title="Viking 1">Viking 1</a></i> in 1976. Twenty years later a rover was landed on Mars by <i><a href="/wiki/Mars_Pathfinder" title="Mars Pathfinder">Mars Pathfinder</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlanetSocMars_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-PlanetSocMars-119">[118]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Outside Mars, Jupiter was first visited by <i><a href="/wiki/Pioneer_10" title="Pioneer 10">Pioneer 10</a></i> in 1973. More than 20 years later <i><a href="/wiki/Galileo_(spacecraft)" title="Galileo (spacecraft)">Galileo</a></i> sent a probe into the planet\'s atmosphere, and became the first spacecraft to orbit the planet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlanetSocJup_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-PlanetSocJup-120">[119]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Pioneer_11" title="Pioneer 11">Pioneer 11</a></i> became the first spacecraft to visit <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a> in 1979, with <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a></i> making the first (and so far only) visits to <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a> in 1986 and 1989, respectively. The first spacecraft to leave the solar system was <i>Pioneer 10</i> in 1983. For a time it was the most distant spacecraft, but it has since been surpassed by both <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_1" title="Voyager 1">Voyager 1</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">Voyager 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JPLVoyager_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-JPLVoyager-121">[120]</a></sup></p>\n<p><i>Pioneers 10</i> and <i>11</i> and both Voyager probes carry messages from the Earth to extraterrestrial life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAPioneer10_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAPioneer10-122">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JPLGolden_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-JPLGolden-123">[122]</a></sup> Communication can be difficult with deep space travel. For instance, it took about three hours for a radio signal to reach the <i>New Horizons</i> spacecraft when it was more than halfway to Pluto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HeavensAbove_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-HeavensAbove-124">[123]</a></sup> Contact with <i>Pioneer 10</i> was lost in 2003. Both Voyager probes continue to operate as they explore the outer boundary between the Solar System and interstellar space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAVoyagesBeyond_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAVoyagesBeyond-125">[124]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On November 26, 2011, NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">Mars Science Laboratory</a> mission was successfully launched for Mars. <i><a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(rover)" title="Curiosity (rover)">Curiosity</a></i> successfully landed on Mars on August 6, 2012, and subsequently began its search for evidence of past or present life on Mars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-MSL_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-MSL-126">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-MSL_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-MSL-127">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_York_Times_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Times-128">[127]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_and_planned_activities">Recent and planned activities</span></h3>\n<p>NASA\'s ongoing investigations include in-depth surveys of Mars (<a href="/wiki/Mars_2020" title="Mars 2020">Mars 2020</a> and <a href="/wiki/InSight" title="InSight">InSight</a>) and Saturn and studies of the Earth and the Sun. Other active spacecraft missions are <i><a href="/wiki/Juno_(spacecraft)" title="Juno (spacecraft)">Juno</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a>, <i>New Horizons</i> (for Jupiter, <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a>, and beyond), and <i><a href="/wiki/Dawn_(spacecraft)" title="Dawn (spacecraft)">Dawn</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_belt" title="Asteroid belt">asteroid belt</a>. NASA continued to support <i><a href="/wiki/In_situ#Space-related" title="In situ">in situ</a></i> exploration beyond the asteroid belt, including Pioneer and Voyager traverses into the unexplored trans-Pluto region, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gas_Giant" title="Gas Giant">Gas Giant</a> orbiters <i>Galileo</i> (1989\xe2\x80\x932003), <i><a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini\xe2\x80\x93Huygens">Cassini</a></i>(1997\xe2\x80\x932017), and <i>Juno</i> (2011\xe2\x80\x93).</p>\n<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a></i> mission to Pluto was launched in 2006 and successfully performed a flyby of <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a> on July 14, 2015. The probe received a <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">gravity assist</a> from <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a> in February 2007, examining some of Jupiter\'s inner moons and testing on-board instruments during the flyby. On the horizon of NASA\'s plans is the <i><a href="/wiki/MAVEN" title="MAVEN">MAVEN</a></i> spacecraft as part of the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Scout_Program" title="Mars Scout Program">Mars Scout Program</a> to study the <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars" title="Atmosphere of Mars">atmosphere of Mars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MAVEN_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-MAVEN-129">[128]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1350" data-file-width="1090" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg/220px-Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg/330px-Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg/440px-Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Innovative_Interstellar_Explorer_interstellar_space_probe_.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nVision mission for an interstellar precursor spacecraft by NASA</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On December 4, 2006, NASA announced it was planning a <a href="/wiki/Lunar_outpost_(NASA)" title="Lunar outpost (NASA)">permanent moon base</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moon2_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-moon2-130">[129]</a></sup> The goal was to start building the moon base by 2020, and by 2024, have a fully functional base that would allow for crew rotations and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In-situ_resource_utilization" title="In-situ resource utilization">in-situ resource utilization</a>. However, in 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Review_of_United_States_Human_Space_Flight_Plans_Committee" title="Review of United States Human Space Flight Plans Committee">Augustine Committee</a> found the program to be on an "unsustainable trajectory."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> In 2010, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> halted existing plans, including the Moon base, and directed a generic focus on manned missions to asteroids and Mars, as well as extending support for the International Space Station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Since 2011, NASA\'s strategic goals have been<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NP-2011-01-699-HQ_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-NP-2011-01-699-HQ-133">[132]</a></sup></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Extend and sustain <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">human activities</a> across the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_system" title="Solar system">solar system</a></li>\n<li>Expand scientific understanding of the Earth and the universe</li>\n<li>Create innovative new space <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technologies" title="Technologies">technologies</a></li>\n<li>Advance <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics" title="Aeronautics">aeronautics</a> research</li>\n<li>Enable program and institutional capabilities to conduct NASA\'s aeronautics and space activities</li>\n<li>Share NASA with the public, educators, and students to provide opportunities to participate</li>\n</ul>\n<p>In August 2011, NASA accepted the donation of <a href="/wiki/2012_National_Reconnaissance_Office_space_telescope_donation_to_NASA" title="2012 National Reconnaissance Office space telescope donation to NASA">two space telescopes</a> from the <a href="/wiki/National_Reconnaissance_Office" title="National Reconnaissance Office">National Reconnaissance Office</a>. Despite being stored unused, the instruments are superior to the <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popsci-2012_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-popsci-2012-134">[133]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In September 2011, NASA announced the start of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">Space Launch System</a> program to develop a human-rated heavy lift vehicle. The Space Launch System is intended to launch the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_Multi-Purpose_Crew_Vehicle" title="Orion Multi-Purpose Crew Vehicle">Orion Multi-Purpose Crew Vehicle</a> and other elements towards the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near-Earth_asteroids" title="Near-Earth asteroids">near-Earth asteroids</a>, and one day <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> The Orion MPCV conducted an unmanned test launch on a <a href="/wiki/Delta_IV_Heavy" title="Delta IV Heavy">Delta IV Heavy</a> rocket in December 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/James_Webb_Space_Telescope" title="James Webb Space Telescope">James Webb Space Telescope</a> (JWST) is currently scheduled to launch in spring 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-launch_2019_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-launch_2019-137">[136]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1200" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg/220px-Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg/330px-Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg/440px-Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martian_gravel_beneath_one_of_the_wheels_of_the_Curiosity_rover.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(rover)" title="Curiosity (rover)"><i>Curiosity</i></a>\'s wheel on <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>, 2012</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On August 6, 2012, NASA landed the rover <i><a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(rover)" title="Curiosity (rover)">Curiosity</a></i> on Mars. On August 27, 2012, <i>Curiosity</i> transmitted the first pre-recorded message from the surface of Mars back to Earth, made by Administrator Charlie Bolden:</p>\n<blockquote class="templatequote">\n<p>Hello. This is Charlie Bolden, NASA Administrator, speaking to you via the broadcast capabilities of the <i>Curiosity</i> Rover, which is now on the surface of Mars.</p>\n<p>Since the beginning of time, humankind\xe2\x80\x99s curiosity has led us to constantly seek new life...new possibilities just beyond the horizon. I want to congratulate the men and women of our NASA family as well as our commercial and government partners around the world, for taking us a step beyond to Mars.<br/>\nThis is an extraordinary achievement. Landing a rover on Mars is not easy\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 others have tried\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 only America has fully succeeded. The investment we are making...the knowledge we hope to gain from our observation and analysis of Gale Crater, will tell us much about the possibility of life on Mars as well as the past and future possibilities for our own planet. <i>Curiosity</i> will bring benefits to Earth and inspire a new generation of scientists and explorers, as it prepares the way for a human mission in the not too distant future. Thank you.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup></p>\n</blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_research">Scientific research</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg/220px-Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg/330px-Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg/440px-Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fueling_of_the_MSL_MMRTG_001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nRadioisotope within a graphite shell that goes into the generator.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NASA_research" title="NASA research">NASA research</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For technologies funded or otherwise supported by NASA, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_spin-off_technologies" title="NASA spin-off technologies">NASA spin-off technologies</a>.</div>\n<p>NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics_Research_Mission_Directorate" title="Aeronautics Research Mission Directorate">Aeronautics Research Mission Directorate</a> conducts aeronautics research.</p>\n<p>NASA has made use of technologies such as the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-Mission_Radioisotope_Thermoelectric_Generator" title="Multi-Mission Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator">Multi-Mission Radioisotope Thermoelectric Generator</a></i> (MMRTG), which is a type of <a href="/wiki/Radioisotope_thermoelectric_generator" title="Radioisotope thermoelectric generator">Radioisotope thermoelectric generator</a> used on space missions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> Shortages of this material have curtailed deep space missions since the turn of the millennia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lpi.usra.edu_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-lpi.usra.edu-140">[139]</a></sup> An example of a spacecraft that was not developed because of a shortage of this material was <i><a href="/wiki/New_Horizons_2" title="New Horizons 2">New Horizons 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lpi.usra.edu_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-lpi.usra.edu-140">[139]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The earth science research program was created and first funded in the 1980s under the administrations of <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_H.W._Bush" title="George H.W. Bush">George H.W. Bush</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup></p>\n<p>NASA started an annual competition in 2014 named <i>Cubes in Space</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> It is jointly organized by NASA and the global education company <i>I Doodle Learning</i>, with the objective of teaching school students aged 11\xe2\x80\x9418 to design and build scientific experiments to be launched into space on a NASA rocket or balloon. On June 21, 2017 the world\'s smallest satellite, <a href="/wiki/Kalam_SAT" title="Kalam SAT">Kalam SAT</a>, built by an Indian team, was launched.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_study">Climate study</span></h3>\n<p>NASA also researches and publishes on <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> Its statements concur with the interpretation that the global climate is heating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Smith_Walker" title="Robert Smith Walker">Bob Walker</a>, who has advised the 45th President of the United States <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> on space issues, has advocated that NASA should focus on space exploration and that its climate study operations should be transferred to other agencies such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">NOAA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:348px;max-width:348px">\n<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:172px;max-width:172px">\n<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg"><img alt="Jet Propulsion Laboratory complex in Pasadena, California" data-file-height="2242" data-file-width="2867" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg/170px-Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg/255px-Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg/340px-Site_du_JPL_en_Californie.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a> complex in Pasadena, California</div>\n</div>\n<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:172px;max-width:172px">\n<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg"><img alt="Vehicle Assembly Building and Launch Control Center at Kennedy Space Center" data-file-height="1151" data-file-width="1499" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg/170px-Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg/255px-Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg/340px-Vehicle-Assembly-Building-July-6-2005.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Vehicle Assembly and Launch Control at <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">Kennedy Space Center</a></div>\n</div>\n<div style="clear:left"></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NASA_facilities" title="NASA facilities">NASA facilities</a></div>\n<p>NASA\'s facilities are research, construction and communication centers to help its missions. Some facilities serve more than one application for historic or administrative reasons. NASA also operates a short-line <a href="/wiki/NASA_Railroad" title="NASA Railroad">railroad at the Kennedy Space Center</a> and own special aircraft, for instance two <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Carrier_Aircraft" title="Shuttle Carrier Aircraft">Boeing 747 that transport Space Shuttle orbiter</a>.</p>\n<p>John F. Kennedy Space Center (KSC), is one of the best-known NASA facilities. It has been the launch site for every United States human space flight since 1968. Although such flights are currently on pause, KSC continues to manage and operate unmanned rocket launch facilities for America\'s civilian space program from three pads at the adjoining Cape Canaveral Air Force Station.</p>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center</a> (JSC) in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center</a>, where all flight control is managed for manned space missions. JSC is the lead NASA center for activities regarding the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> and also houses the <a href="/wiki/NASA_Astronaut_Corps" title="NASA Astronaut Corps">NASA Astronaut Corps</a> that selects, trains, and provides astronauts as crew members for US and international space missions.</p>\n<p>Another major facility is <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="Marshall Space Flight Center">Marshall Space Flight Center</a> in Huntsville, Alabama at which the Saturn 5 rocket and Skylab were developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAMSFC_Fact_sheet_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAMSFC_Fact_sheet-147">[146]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">JPL</a> worked together with <a href="/wiki/Army_Ballistic_Missile_Agency" title="Army Ballistic Missile Agency">ABMA</a>, one of the agencies behind <a href="/wiki/Explorer_1" title="Explorer 1">Explorer 1</a>, the first American space mission.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg/220px-STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg/330px-STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg/440px-STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-128_MCC_space_station_flight_control_room.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center#FCR_1_.282006-present.29" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">FCR 1</a> in 2009 during the <a href="/wiki/STS-128" title="STS-128">STS-128</a> mission, JSC in Houston</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The ten NASA field centers are:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Space_Center" title="John F. Kennedy Space Center">John F. Kennedy Space Center</a>, Florida</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ames_Research_Center" title="Ames Research Center">Ames Research Center</a>, Moffett Field, California</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Armstrong_Flight_Research_Center" title="Armstrong Flight Research Center">Armstrong Flight Research Center</a> (formerly Hugh L. Dryden Flight Research Facility), Edwards, California</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">Goddard Space Flight Center</a>, Greenbelt, Maryland</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a>, near Pasadena, California</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center</a>, Houston, Texas</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Langley_Research_Center" title="Langley Research Center">Langley Research Center</a>, Hampton, Virginia</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_H._Glenn_Research_Center" title="John H. Glenn Research Center">John H. Glenn Research Center</a>, Cleveland, Ohio</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_C._Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="George C. Marshall Space Flight Center">George C. Marshall Space Flight Center</a>, Huntsville, Alabama</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John_C._Stennis_Space_Center" title="John C. Stennis Space Center">John C. Stennis Space Center</a>, Bay St. Louis, Mississippi</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Numerous other facilities are operated by NASA, including the <a href="/wiki/Wallops_Flight_Facility" title="Wallops Flight Facility">Wallops Flight Facility</a> in Wallops Island, Virginia; the <a href="/wiki/Michoud_Assembly_Facility" title="Michoud Assembly Facility">Michoud Assembly Facility</a> in New Orleans, Louisiana; the <a href="/wiki/White_Sands_Test_Facility" title="White Sands Test Facility">White Sands Test Facility</a> in Las Cruces, New Mexico; and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep_Space_Network" title="Deep Space Network">Deep Space Network</a> stations in <a href="/wiki/Goldstone_Deep_Space_Communications_Complex" title="Goldstone Deep Space Communications Complex">Barstow</a>, California; <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Deep_Space_Communications_Complex" title="Madrid Deep Space Communications Complex">Madrid</a>, Spain; and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canberra_Deep_Space_Communications_Complex" title="Canberra Deep Space Communications Complex">Canberra</a>, Australia.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget">Budget</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NASA-Budget-Federal.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="589" data-file-width="1151" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/NASA-Budget-Federal.svg/220px-NASA-Budget-Federal.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/NASA-Budget-Federal.svg/330px-NASA-Budget-Federal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/NASA-Budget-Federal.svg/440px-NASA-Budget-Federal.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NASA-Budget-Federal.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nNASA\'s budget from 1958 to 2012 as a percentage of federal budget</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jsc2004e18852.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3555" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jsc2004e18852.jpg/220px-Jsc2004e18852.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jsc2004e18852.jpg/330px-Jsc2004e18852.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Jsc2004e18852.jpg/440px-Jsc2004e18852.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jsc2004e18852.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAn artist\'s conception, from NASA, of an astronaut planting a US flag on Mars. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manned_mission_to_Mars" title="Manned mission to Mars">manned mission to Mars</a> has been discussed as a possible NASA mission since the 1960s.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_NASA" title="Budget of NASA">Budget of NASA</a></div>\n<p>NASA\'s budget has generally been approximately 1% of the federal budget from the early 1970s on, after briefly peaking at approximately 4.41% in 1966 during the Apollo program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-28">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> Public perception of NASA\'s budget has differed significantly from reality; a 1997 poll indicated that most Americans responded that 20% of the federal budget went to NASA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perception_of_US_Human_Spaceflight_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-perception_of_US_Human_Spaceflight-149">[148]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The percentage of federal budget that NASA has been allocated has been steadily dropping since the Apollo program and in 2012 it was estimated at 0.48% of the federal budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2013_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-B2013-150">[149]</a></sup> In a March 2012 meeting of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Commerce,_Science_and_Transportation" title="United States Senate Committee on Commerce, Science and Transportation">United States Senate Science Committee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neil_deGrasse_Tyson" title="Neil deGrasse Tyson">Neil deGrasse Tyson</a> testified that "Right now, NASA\xe2\x80\x99s annual budget is half a penny on your tax dollar. For twice that\xe2\x80\x94a penny on a dollar\xe2\x80\x94we can transform the country from a sullen, dispirited nation, weary of economic struggle, to one where it has reclaimed its 20th century birthright to dream of tomorrow."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tysontranscript_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-tysontranscript-151">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tysontranscript_video_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-tysontranscript_video-152">[151]</a></sup></p>\n<p>For Fiscal Year 2015, NASA received an appropriation of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$18.01 billion</span> from Congress\xe2\x80\x94$549 million more than requested and approximately $350 million more than the 2014 NASA budget passed by Congress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20141214_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-sfn20141214-153">[152]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_impact">Environmental impact</span></h2>\n<p>The exhaust gases produced by rocket propulsion systems, both in Earth\'s atmosphere and in space, can adversely effect the Earth\'s environment. Some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypergolic" title="Hypergolic">hypergolic</a> rocket propellants, such as <a href="/wiki/Hydrazine" title="Hydrazine">hydrazine</a>, are highly toxic prior to <a href="/wiki/Combustion" title="Combustion">combustion</a>, but decompose into less toxic compounds after burning. Rockets using hydrocarbon fuels, such as <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a>, release carbon dioxide and soot in their exhaust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rocket_soot_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-rocket_soot-154">[153]</a></sup> However, carbon dioxide emissions are insignificant compared to those from other sources; on average, the United States consumed 802,620,000 US gallons (3.0382<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\xc3\x97</span>10<sup>9</sup>\xc2\xa0L) gallons of liquid fuels per day in 2014, while a single <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9" title="Falcon 9">Falcon 9</a> rocket first stage burns around 25,000 US gallons (95,000\xc2\xa0L) of <a href="/wiki/Kerosene" title="Kerosene">kerosene</a> fuel per launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIA_2016_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-EIA_2016-155">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> Even if a Falcon 9 were launched every single day, it would only represent 0.006% of liquid fuel consumption (and carbon dioxide emissions) for that day. Additionally, the exhaust from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LOx" title="LOx">LOx</a>- and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LH2" title="LH2">LH2</a>- fueled engines, like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SSME" title="SSME">SSME</a>, is almost entirely water vapor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-SSME_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-SSME-157">[156]</a></sup> NASA addressed environmental concerns with its canceled <a href="/wiki/Constellation_program" title="Constellation program">Constellation program</a> in accordance with the National Environmental Policy Act in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-Constellation_Program_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-Constellation_Program-158">[157]</a></sup> In contrast, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ion_engines" title="Ion engines">ion engines</a> use harmless noble gases like <a href="/wiki/Xenon" title="Xenon">xenon</a> for propulsion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ns20070928_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-ns20070928-159">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goto2003_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goto2003-160">[159]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On May 8, 2003, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">Environmental Protection Agency</a> recognized NASA as the first federal agency to directly use <a href="/wiki/Landfill_gas" title="Landfill gas">landfill gas</a> to produce energy at one of its facilities\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">Goddard Space Flight Center</a>, Greenbelt, Maryland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup></p>\n<p>An example of NASA\'s environmental efforts is the <a href="/wiki/NASA_Sustainability_Base" title="NASA Sustainability Base">NASA Sustainability Base</a>. Additionally, the Exploration Sciences Building was awarded the LEED Gold rating in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Observations">Observations</span></h2>\n<center>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n<div style="width: 155px">\n<div mw-gallery-traditional">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n<div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n<div style="margin:29.5px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NASA_spacecraft_comparison.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3559" data-file-width="4669" height="91" class="mw-references-wrap">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-independent_agency-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-independent_agency_10-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">NASA is an independent agency that is not a part of any <a href="/wiki/United_States_federal_executive_departments" title="United States federal executive departments">executive department</a> but reports directly to the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-163"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-163">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">From left to right: Launch vehicle of Apollo (Saturn 5), Gemini (Titan 2) and Mercury (Atlas). Left, top-down: Spacecraft of Apollo, Gemini and Mercury.
